Jamison Brereton

166
Maruts
Agastya Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
15 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 14тАУ15
Many of the usual Marut themes are present in this hymn: the awesome and ter rifying power of the thunderstorm (vss. 4тАУ6), their glittering bedecked bodies and chariots (vss. 9тАУ11), their aid to pious men (vss. 2тАУ3, 7тАУ8), their role as singers for their comrade Indra (vss. 7, 11). Although the order of elements seems somewhat random, these praises are set within a tight frame. Verse 1 begins тАЬwe shall proclaim their greatness,тАЭ which is echoed exactly by verse 12 тАЬthis is your greatnessтАЭ: the promised proclamation has reached its end. Verse 13 is similarly structured, begin ning тАЬthis is your kinship…,тАЭ and the final verse (14) before the refrain sets forth what the poet wishes from the Maruts.
Punctuating the hymn is an awareness of the balance between their past glories and benevolence and the ones of the present day (see esp. vss. 1, 8, 13), and the model of their previous generosity to sacrificers is given embodiment in verse 13, where ManuтАЩs offering of poetry induces the Maruts to appear to him with their favors.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe proclaim eagerly, Maruts, your ancient greatness, for (the sake of inducing) your prompt appearance, as the indication of (the approach of) the showerer (of benefits). Loud-roaring and mighty Maruts, you exert your vigorous energies for the advance (to the sacrifice), as if it was to battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We shall now proclaim this to the overpowering raceтАФproclaim their previous greatness to the beacon of the bull.
As if through kindling on your course, you powerfully noisy Maruts, as if in battle, produce your powers, o able ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It may not be sufficiently clear in the published translation that тАЬthe beacon of the bullтАЭ refers to the Maruts themselves. They are presumably IndraтАЩs тАЬbeaconтАЭ because they are regularly his comrades and they are of glittering appearance – a little bit like Rudolph the Red-nosed Reindeer.

The pair тАЬkindlingтАЭ and тАЬbattleтАЭ in cd may not seem to form a natural class, but they probably represent two aspects of the MarutsтАЩ naturalistic identity as the thunderstorm: the lightning may be the kindling and the thunder the clash of battle.

Note the phonological echoes in aidh├йva…, yudh├йva…; similarly tuviс╣гvaс╣Зo…

Now let us publish, for the vigorous company the herald of the Strong One, their primeval might.
With fire upon your way, O Maruts loud of voice, with battle, Mighty Ones, achieve your deeds of strength.

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН

Ever carrying honey like a son [to] near [us],
the playful (gods) sport, joyful at the ritual assemblies.
The rudra-s come with aid to the worshipper,
self-strong, they do not neglect the offerer of oblations.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬEver accepting the sweet (libation), as (they would) a son, they sport plural playfully at sacrifices, demolishing (all intruders);
the Rudras come to the offerer of prayers and oblations, for his protection, and powerul as they are, do him no harm.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Holding their honey close like their own son, the playful ones play, eager at the rites.
The Rudras [=Maruts] approach the reverent man with help; the
self-powerful ones do not neglect the maker of oblations.

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдпреЗ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рди рдордзреБ рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддрдГ рд╕реВрдиреБрдореБрдк рдХреНрд░реАрд│рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗрд╖реБ рдШреГрд╖реНрд╡рдпрдГ рдХреНрд░реАрд│рд╛ рдирдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрд┐ рд░реБрджреНрд░рд╛рдЗрд╡рд╛рд╡рд╕рд╛ рдирдорд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдВ рди рдорд░реНрджреНрдзрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рддрд╡рд╕реЛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдХреГрддрдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдиреНрдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рд╕реЗрд╡рдзреНрд╡рдореН рее реи рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдореН) рдирд╛рд╢рд░рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдЬреАрд╡рдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд╕реВрдиреБрдореН) рдЕрдкрддреНрдпрдореН (рдордзреБ) рдордзреБрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддрдГ) рдзрд░рддрдГ (рдЙрдк) рд╕рд╛рдореАрдкреНрдпреЗ (рдХреНрд░реАрд│рдиреНрддрд┐) (рдХреНрд░реАрд│рд╛рдГ) рдХреНрд░реАрдбрдХрд╛рдГ (рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗрд╖реБ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ (рдШреГрд╖реНрд╡рдпрдГ) рд╕реЛрдврд╛рд░рдГ (рдирдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рд░реБрджреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛ рдЗрд╡ (рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреНрдпреЗрди (рдирдорд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдореН) рдмрд╣реНрд╡рдиреНрдирдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рди) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рдорд░реНрджреНрдзрдиреНрддрд┐) рдпреЛрдзрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ (рд╕реНрд╡рддрд╡рд╕рдГ) рд╕реНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрдВ рддрд╡реЛ рдмрд▓рдВ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдиреНрддреЗ (рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдХреГрддрдореН) рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрднрд┐рд░реНрджрд╛рдиреИрд░реНрдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрдореН рее реи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдпрд╕реНрдореИ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛ рджрджрд╛рд╢реБрд╖реЗ рд╕реЛрдорд╛рджрд┐рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрджрддреНрддрд╡рддреЗ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛ рдкреНрд░реАрддрд╛рдГ рдКрдорд╛рд╕рдГ рдЕрд╡рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдГ рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рдГ рдЕрдорд░рдгрдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдгреЛ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд░рд╛рдпрд╕реНрдкреЛрд╖рдВ рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдореН ред рдЪрд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рддреН рдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдореН ред рдЕрд░рд╛рд╕рдд рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН ред рд░рд╛рд╕рддрд┐рд░реНрджрд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдЗрд╡ рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдЪрд░рдгрд╛рдГ рд╕рдЦрд╛рдп рдЗрд╡ рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ рдордпреЛрднреБрд╡рдГ рд╕реБрдЦрд╕реНрдп рднрд╛рд╡рдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдГ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд░рдЬрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдиреН рдкреБрд░реБ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрдВ рдпрдерд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдкрдпрд╕рд╛ рдЙрджрдХреЗрди рд╕рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпреБрддреНрдкрддреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердореН рдЙрдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕рд┐рдЮреНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐ рееред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo him, the presenter (of offerings), the protecting and immortal Maruts, (gratified) by the oblation, have given abundance of riches; they, the bestowers of happiness, becoming, as it were, the friends (of the worshipper), sprinkle the regions plural ntifully with water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To whom the immortal helpers have given riches and prosperityтАФto the man who does pious service with the oblationтАФ
for him the Maruts, like (steeds) spurred on, sprinkle the many realms with milkтАФthey are joy itself.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The simile hit─Б╠Бiva is compared by Geldner and Renou with a similar expression in IV.57.1, with the meaning тАЬgood (friends)тАЭ (Geldner тАЬwie gute (Freunde)тАЭ) or, more technically, тАЬlike contracted (allies)тАЭ (see the bahuvr─лhi hit├б-mitra-). This doesnтАЩt mean much in the context here. Witzel Got┼Н are somewhat skeptical, but simply tr. literally тАЬwie die HingesetztenтАЭ without explaining what that might mean here. Both the Geldner/Renou and the Witzel Got┼Н tr. assume a ppl. to тИЪdh─Б тАШset, establishтАЩ. I take it rather to тИЪhi тАШimpelтАЩ (as does Grassmann) and assume that the underlying subject is horses and that the image is of horses led out to piss before contests. See esp. I.64.6 (also a Marut hymn) ├бtyaс╣Г n├б mih├й v├н nayanti v─Бj├нnam тАЬThey lead (their horse) out to piss like a prizeseeking steedтАЭ (also cf. II.34.13, IX.74.4). This image fits well with the sprinkling here.

Griffith

To whomsoever, bringer of oblations, they immortal guardians, have given plenteous wealth,
For him, like loving friends, the Maruts bringing bliss bedew the regions round with milk abundantly.

Geldner

Wem die unsterblichen Helfer Reicht├╝mer und Zuwachs gew├дhrt haben, weil er mit Opfer freigebig war, f├╝r den besprengen die Marut wie gute Freunde viele Landstrecken mit Milch, die Erquickenden.

Grassmann

Wem Gut und Nahrung schenkten die unsterblichen Genossen, wenn mit Opfertrank er huldiget, Dem netzen sie, die Maruts, die erquickenden, mit fetter Milch die vielen Fluren Freunden gleich.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThose, your coursers, which traverse the regions in their speed, proceed, self-guided; all worlds, all dwellings, are alarmed, for marvellous is your coming; (such fear as is felt) when spears are thrust forth (in battle).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Of you who with your powers enveloped the realmsтАФyour spontaneous dashes swooped forth.
All creatures and habitations take fright. Brilliant is your course when your spears have been extended.

Griffith

Ye who with mighty powers have stirred the regions up, your coursers have sped forth directed by themselves.
All creatures of the earth, all dwellings are afraid, for brilliant is your coming with your spears advanced.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen your brilliant coursers make the mountains echo; and, friendly to man, traverse the summit of the firmament; then all the forest lords are alarmed at your approach, and the bushes wave to and fro, as a woman in a chariot.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When the manly ones of turbulent course make the mountains roar, or have stirred the back of heaven,
every tree takes fright at your drive; every plant bends forward as if driving a chariot.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I previously (1983: 61) took nadayanta as intransitive тАЬthey roared and made the mountains stir тАжтАЭ, but I now accept a transitive value.

Griffith

When they in dazzling rush have made the mountains roar, and shaken heaven’s high back in their heroic strength,
Each sovran of the forest fears as ye drive near, aid the shrubs fly before you swift as whirling wheels.

Geldner

Wenn die Mannschaften in hitzigem Anlauf die Berge erdr├╢hnen machen oder des Himmels R├╝cken ersch├╝ttert haben, dann bebt jeder Baum bei eurem Ansturm. Das Kraut eilt voraus, als ob es eine Wettfahrt machte.

Grassmann

Wenn sie ersch├╝ttern wilden Laufs die Bergesh├╢hn, und auch des Himmels R├╝cken vor den Helden bebt, Dann zittert jeder Waldesbaum bei eurer Fahrt, wie Wagenlenker weichen alle Kr├дuter aus.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFierce Maruts, free from malevolence in your kindly thoughts, fulfil towards us your good purposes; when your missile lightning rends (the clouds), as a well-hurled weapon wound the deer.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Asa a well-hurled weapon: pa┼Ыvaс╕е sudhiteva barhaс╣З─Б: pa┼Ы┼лn is connected with with krivirdat─л, the missile of the winds; when the wind blows, animals are withered or chilled

Jamison Brereton

You, mighty Maruts, you invulnerable bandтАФwith kind attention deliver us to your benevolence.
Where your missile with its gory teeth scrapes (a path), mightily it
liquefies (the trees) as a well-placed (goad) sets the livestock flowing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

├бriс╣гс╣нagr─Бm─Бс╕е is a bahuvr─лhi, but the tr. тАШhaving an invulnerable bandтАЩ seemed too heavy.

On kr├нvis- see comm. to I.30.1, where I suggest a relationship with krav├нs- тАШraw, bloody fleshтАЩ as a re-formed -i-stem to the underlying root kr┼л тЖР *kruH. A number of other interpr. have been made.

I supply тАЬ(a path)тАЭ as obj. of r├бdati because words for тАШpath, wayтАЩ are frequently obj. of this verb (e.g., VII.87.1 r├бdat path├бс╕е; also II.30.2, V.10.1, V.80.3, VI.30.3, VII.47.4, VII.60.4, X.75.2).

In my reading the structure of p─Бda d is quite complex and intricate and differs from the standard. Both Geldner and Renou supply тАШwatersтАЩ as the obj. of riс╣З─Б╠Бti in the frame (see also Oldenberg), since waters are several times elsewhere the obj. of тИЪr─л. (Witzel Got┼Н take pa┼Ыv├бс╕е as obj. of both simile and frame.) I prefer to find the object nearer at hand, namely trees, based on v├бnaspati(с╕е) in the previous vs. (5c). In another passage trees liquefy at the MarutsтАЩ assault: V.58.6 тАж riс╣Зat├й v├бn─Бni, and a transitive version of this phrase is found with Agni as subj. at V.41.10 n├н riс╣З─Бti v├бn─Б (cf. I.127.4).

As for the simile, Geldner takes barh├бс╣З─Б as fem. nom. sg. with s├║dhit─Б (тАЬwie der beharrliche Eifer тАжтАЭ), but barh├бс╣З─Б, which is fairly well attested, is otherwise only an instr. sg. used adverbially (so rendered by both Renou and Witzel Got┼Н). Like Renou and Witzel Got┼Н I take didy├║t (fem.) of c as the referent of s├║dhit─Б тАШwell-placedтАЩ, but didy├║t- in a slightly different sense: not as a thrown missile but as a sharp-pointed thing used as a goad. The verb riс╣З─Б╠Бti is held constant between simile and frame, but again it has different senses in the two structures: in the simile it does not mean тАШliquefy, dissolve, i.e., destroyтАЩ, but тАШmake to flow, i.e., to cause to moveтАЩ, a more appropriate meaning with pa┼Ыv├бс╕е тАШlivestockтАЩ as object.

Griffith

Terrible Maruts, ye with ne’er-diminished host, with great benevolence fulfil our heart’s desire.
Where’er your lightning bites armed with its gory teeth it crunches up the cattle like a well-aimed dart.

Geldner

Ihr gewaltige Marut mit unversehrter Schar, schenket uns wohlwollend eure Gnade in F├╝lle! Wo euer Gescho├Я mit dem feuerfarbenen Zahn furcht, da macht es die Wasser frei, wie der beharrliche Eifer die Herdentiere.

Grassmann

O starke Maruts, ihr mit unversehrter Schar, erf├╝llet unser Wunschgebet mit holdem Sinn; Wo euer Blitz mit seinen blut’gen Z├дhnen beisst, zermalmt er Heerden wie ein wohlgezielter Pfeil.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGivers without stint, possessors of inexhaustible riches, devoid of malevolence, ever glorified at sacrifices, they worship the adorable (Indra), for (the sake of) drinking (the Soma) wine; for they know the first manly exploits of the hero.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(The Maruts) whose generosity is (as steady as) a pillar, whose gifts are not withdrawn, the restless ones, well-praised at the ritesтАФ
they chant forth the chant for the drinking of the exhilarating (soma); they know the foremost manly deeds of the hero [=Indra].

Jamison Brereton Notes

The rendering of al─Бtс╣Ыс╣З├б- as тАШrestlessтАЩ follows the suggestion of HoffmannтАЩs (тАШunruhigтАЩ) registered in KEWA III.807 and EWA s.v., derived from тИЪr─Б тАШbe at restтАЩ.

The word is found elsewhere only in III.30.10, of Vala. In neither passage does тАШunquiet, restlessтАЩ fit the context terribly well, but in neither is it excluded. Kuiper (Aryans, 84-85, in part restating his 1955 Fs. Kirfel views) objects to HoffmannтАЩs explanation and suggests instead the meaning тАШirresistibleтАЩ for our passage and тАШnot offering resistanceтАЩ for III.30.10. (On a side note, these two meanings, reflecting passive тАШnot (to be) resistedтАЩ and active тАШnot resistingтАЩ senses respectively, do not seem to me derivationally compatible and should not be found in a single word.) He considers it to be a substrate borrowing and thinks itтАЩs not realistic to expect it to have an etymology. Kuiper has some good points: as was just noted, the meaning produced by the Hoffmann etymology is not a perfect fit contextually and the morphology is somewhat dubious. However, I do not see confidently proposing two incompatible meanings for a single word (with the one suggested for this passage not particularly compelling in context) while forswearing any attempt at etymology.

Better to leave it untranslated in that case.

P─Бdas c and d are in reverse logical order. The contents of the chant that the Maruts chant (c) must be the deeds of Indra, which they are said to know (d); the knowledge logically precedes the verbal expression of it.

Griffith

Givers of during gifts whose bounties never fail, free from ill-will, at sacrifices glorified,
They sing their song aloud that they may drink sweet juice: well do they know the Hero’s first heroic deeds.

Geldner

Sie, deren Gaben nicht wankend wie die S├дulen, deren Geschenke nicht zu entrei├Яen sind, die nicht zur├╝ckfordern, die in weisen Reden gefeierten, sie singen den Gesang, um vom berauschenden Soma trinken zu d├╝rfen; sie kennen des Helden erste Heldentaten.

Grassmann

Sie, deren Gaben fest sind, deren Lohn nicht weicht, beim Fest gepriesen, deren G├╝ter niemand raubt, Sie lassen Sang erschallen zu des Soma Trunk; des Helden erste Mannesthaten kennen sie.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╢рддрднреБрдЬрд┐рднрд┐рдГ ред рд╢рддрдорд┐рддреНрдпрдкрд░рд┐рдорд┐рддрдирд╛рдо ред рдЕрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрднреЛрдЧрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рдкреВрд░реНрднрд┐рдГ рдкрд╛рд▓рдиреИрдГ рдЬреЗрддрд╡реНрдпреИрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдирдЧрд░реИрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рддрдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдд рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрдд ред рддрдорд┐рддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рдХрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ ред рдпрдореН рдЬрдирдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд╣реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ рдЕрднрд┐рднрд╡рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рддреН рдХреБрдЯрд┐рд▓рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рддреН рдЕрдШрд╛рддреН рдкрд╛рдкрд╛рддреН рдЖрд╡рдд рдЕрд░рдХреНрд╖рдд ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рд╣реЗ рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдЙрджреНрдЧреВрд░реНрдгрддреЗрдЬрд╕реЛ рд╣реЗ рддрд╡рд╕рдГ рдмрд▓рд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡реЗрдЧрд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рд╛ рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рд░рдкреНрд╢рд┐рдирдГ ред рдорд╣рдиреНрдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рд░рдкрдгреАрдпрд╛: рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдГ рд░рдкрд╛рдГред рддреЗ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддреЗ рд░рдкреНрд╢рд┐рдирдГ ред рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛ рд░рдкреНрд╢рд┐рдирдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░реЛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддреЗ рддрдереЛрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╣реЗ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рд╛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдпрдВ рдЪ рдЬрдирдВ рдкрд╛рдерди рдкрд╛рде рд░рдХреНрд╖рде ред рдХрд╕реНрдорд╛рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрдирдпрд╕реНрдп ред рдЙрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдореЗрддрддреН ред рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд╖реБ рдкреЛрд╖реЗрд╖реБ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрднреВрддреЗрд╖реБ рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рддреН рдЕрднрд┐рд╢рдВрд╕рдирд╛рддреН ред рдпрдореЗрд╡рдВ рдХреБрд░реБрде рддрдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рддреЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рее рдкрд╛рдкрдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛рджреНрдпрдирд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдкрд░рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░реЗрдг рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдкреЛрд╖рд░реВрдкреЗрд╖реНрдЯрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рдЪ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдереЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, gratify, with infinite and complete enjoyments, him, whom you proect from degrading sin; that man whom, fierce and mighty, and glorified (as you are), you defend from calumny, by (providing for) the nourishment of his descendants.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Of his descendants: tanayasya puс╣гс╣нiс╣гu: tanaya, a son = putr─Бdayaс╕е, descendants

Jamison Brereton

With your strongholds with a hundred coils, o Maruts, guard that man from crookedness and evil whom you (previously) aided,
whom you (now) protect from (evil) utterance amid the flourishing of his descendants, you mighty, powerful ones who confer abundance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As pointed out, e.g., by Geldner, ┼Ы├бс╣Гs─Бt in d must stand for *agh─Б╠Бd ┼Ы├бс╣Гs─Бt тАЬfrom evil utterance,тАЭ borrowing the agh─Б╠Бt of p─Бda a (and cf. the bahuvr─лhi agh├б┼Ыaс╣Гsa- тАШof evil speechтАЩ, referring to the utterer thereof). It may well be (with Geldner, etc.) that ┼Ы├бс╣Гs─Бt should likewise be supplied in a, but тАЬguard from evil,тАЭ without the addition of тАЬutterance,тАЭ is also perfectly acceptable.

Griffith

With castles hundredfold, O Maruts, guard ye well the man whom ye have loved from ruin and from sin,–
The man whom ye the fierce, the Mighty ones who roar, preserve from calumny by cherishing his seed.

Geldner

Mit hundertfachen Burgen bewahret den, o Marut, wem ihr eure Gunst geschenkt habt, vor R├дnken, vor b├╢sem Gerede! Welchem Mann ihr Gewaltigen, Starken, Reichen eure Gunst geschenkt habt, den sch├╝tzet ihr vor b├╢sem Gerede in gedeihlichem Besitz von Nachkommenschaft.

Grassmann

Mit hunderfach umschanzten Burgen schirmt den Mann, vor Leid und Noth, o Maruts, den erquickt ihr habt, Den ihr, o starke, m├дcht’ge, die ihr strotzt von Kraft, vor Fluch bewahrt und seinem Stamm Gedeihen schafft.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рддрдирдпрд╕реНрдп) рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рди рдХреА (рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд╖реБ) рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХрд╛рдореЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА рддреАрд╡реНрд░ рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдкрдпреБрдХреНрдд (рддрд╡рд╕рдГ) рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрдд рдмрдврд╝реЗ рд╣реБрдП рдмрд▓ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рд╡рд┐рд░рдкреНрд╢рд┐рдирдГ) рдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдФрд░ рдкреВрд░реНрдг рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдорд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рдкрд╡рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛ ! рддреБрдо (рд╢рддрднреБрдЬрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рдЕрд╕рдЩреНрдЦреНрдп рд╕реБрдЦ рднреЛрдЧрдиреЗ рдХреЛ рдЬрд┐рдирдХрд╛ рд╢реАрд▓ (рдкреВрд░реНрднрд┐рдГ) рдкреВрд░рдг, рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдФрд░ рд╕реБрдЦрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдирдЧрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рдпрдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреА (рдЕрднрд┐рд╣реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рдХреБрдЯрд┐рд▓ (рдЕрдШрд╛рддреН) рдкрд╛рдк рд╕реЗ (рд░рдХреНрд╖рдд) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░реЛ рдмрдЪрд╛рдУ рд╡рд╛ (рдпрдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕ (рдЬрдирдореН) рдЬрди рдХреЛ (рдЖрд╡рдд) рдкрд╛рд▓реЛ рд╡рд╛ рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреА (рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рддреН) рдЖрддреНрдордкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реВрдк рджреЛрд╖ рд╕реЗ (рдкрд╛рдерди) рдкрд╛рд▓рдирд╛ рдХрд░реЛ (рддрдореН) рдЙрд╕рдХреА рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ рднреА рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рее рео рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЖрд╣рд╛рд░-рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░, рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛, рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдп рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрдд, рд╕рддреНрдп рдХреА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдФрд░ рдкрд╛рдк рд╕реЗ рдЕрд▓рдЧ рд░рд╣рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХрд░рддреЗ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдг рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдХреЛ рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд┐рдд рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рдЕрдирдиреНрдд рд╕реБрдЦрднреЛрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее рео рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рддрдирдпрд╕реНрдп рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рдпрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрддрд╡рд╕реЛ рд╡рд┐рд░рдкреНрд╢рд┐рдиреЛ рдорд░реБрддреЛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╢рддрднреБрдЬрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкреВрд░реНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рдпрдорднрд┐рд╣реНрд░реБрддреЗрд░рдШрд╛рджреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рдд рдпрдВ рдЬрдирдорд╛рд╡рдд рдпрдВ рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рддреНрдкрд╛рдерди рддрдВ рд╡рдпрдордкрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рд░рдХреНрд╖реЗрдо рее рео рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╢рддрднреБрдЬрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рд╢рддрдорд╕рдЩреНрдЦреНрдпрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рднреЛрдХреНрддреБрдВ рд╢реАрд▓рдВ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдиреНрддреИрдГ (рддрдореН) (рдЕрднрд┐рд╣реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ) рдЕрднрд┐рддрдГ рдХреБрдЯрд┐рд▓рд╛рддреН (рдЕрдШрд╛рддреН) рдкрд╛рдкрд╛рддреН (рдкреВрд░реНрднрд┐рдГ) рдкреВрд░рдгрдкрд╛рд▓рдирд╕реБрдЦрдпреБрдХреНрддреИрд░реНрдирдЧрд░реИрдГ (рд░рдХреНрд╖рдд)ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рд╜рдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдордкреАрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рд╡рд╛рдпрд╡рдЗрд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ (рдпрдореН) (рдЖрд╡рдд) рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрдд (рдЬрдирдореН) (рдпрдореН) (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдГ (рддрд╡рд╕рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдмрд▓рд╛рдГ (рд╡рд┐рд░рдкреНрд╢рд┐рдирдГ) рдкреВрд░реНрдгрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рдкрд╛рдерди) рд░рдХреНрд╖рддред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдордкреАрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рддреН) рдЖрддреНрдорд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд░реВрдкрд╛рддреН рджреЛрд╖рд╛рддреН (рддрдирдпрд╕реНрдп) рдЕрдкрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп (рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд╖реБ) рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХрд░рдгреЗрд╖реБ рдХрд░реНрдореНрдорд╕реБ рее рео рее

рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд╡рдГ рд░рдереЗрд╖реБ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорддреНрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рд░рдереЗрд╖реБ рд░рдВрд╣рдгрд╕рд╛рдзрдиреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ рднрджреНрд░рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдирд┐ рднреЛрдЧрдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдгреНрдпрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рджреЗрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдлрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╡рдГ рдЕрдВрд╕реЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╛ рддрджреБрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрднреБрдЬреЗрд╖реНрд╡рдкрд┐ ред рдЖрдХрд╛рд░реЛрд╜рдкреНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ ред рдорд┐рдерд╕реНрдкреГрдзреНрдпреЗрд╡ рдмрд▓рд╛рдзрд┐рдХреНрдпрд╛рддреН рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рддрд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛рдгрд┐ рдмрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрдВрд╕реЗрд╖реВрдХреНрддрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдзрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд╛ рдЖрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рд╡рдГ рдкреНрд░рдкрдереЗрд╖реБ ред рдкреНрд░рдЧрддрд╛рдГ рдкрдиреНрдерд╛рдиреЛ рдпреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд░рд╛рдорд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╖реБ рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рдкрдерд╛рдирд┐ ред рддреЗрд╖реБ рдЦрд╛рджрдпрдГ рдЦрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рднрдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгреНрдпрд╛рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдкреНрд░рдЧрддрдГ рдкрдиреНрдерд╛ рдпреИрд╕реНрддреЗрд╖реБ рдкрд╛рджрд╛рдЧреНрд░реЗрд╖реБ рдЦрд╛рджрдпрдГ рд╕реНрдерд┐рд░рд╛ рдЖрднрд░рдгрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛ рдЖрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдГ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдЕрдХреНрд╖реЛ рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорддреНрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреА рд░рдереНрдпрдГ рдЕрдХреНрд╖рдГ рдЪрдХреНрд░рд╛ рддрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдирд┐рдмрджреНрдзрд╛рдирд┐ рдЪрдХреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕рдордпрд╛ рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рд╕рд░реЗ рд╡рд┐ рд╡рд╡реГрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рди рдХрджрд╛рдЪрд┐рджрдкрд┐ рдЪрдХреНрд░реЗрд╖реБ рд╕рдВрд▓рдЧреНрдиреЛ рднрд╡рддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреЗрд╡рдВ рджреЗрд╡рдпрдЬрдирдЧрдордирд╕рд╛рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдорд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдзреНрд╡рдорд┐рддреНрдпрднрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, all good things are in your cars; on your shoulders abides emulous strength; at your resting-plural ces on the road refreshments (are ready); the axle of your (chariot) wheels holds them firmly together.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

At your resting plural ces: prapatheс╣гu kh─Бdayaс╕е, an indication of facilities for shelter and provisions to travellers

Jamison Brereton

All good things are set on your chariots, MarutsтАФlike powers competing with each other.364 I.167
On your shoulders, in the vanguard, are spangles; your axle turns the wheels separately but at the same time.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou make taviс╣г─Б╠Бс╣Зi part of the frame, not the simile. This actually does not alter the sense very much, since they still read mithaspс╣Ы╠Бdhy─Б with taviс╣г─Б╠Бс╣Зi in an тАЬas ifтАЭ construction. Given the structure of the hemistich and the need for something for mithaspс╣Ы╠Бdhy─Б to modify, I prefer to take it with the simile. My only reservation about putting taviс╣г─Б╠Бс╣Зi in the simile is that the MarutsтАЩ taviс╣г─Б╠Бс╣Зi are mentioned in 1d.

More crucial is the grammatical identity and function of mithaspс╣Ы╠Бdhy─Б (so Pp.). Oldenberg follows BR in taking this not as a gerundive but as a gerund, but, strikingly, neither suggests a tr. for it. Since a simile consisting of a gerund would be highly unusual (unprecedented, I think, though I havenтАЩt checked the entire RV), a neut. pl.

gerundive agreeing with taviс╣г─Б╠Бс╣Зi makes more grammatical sense. But what meaning is being conveyed? I think the point is that there are so many good things on the chariot that one canтАЩt single out just one: like opposing forces (taviс╣г─Б╠Бс╣Зi) they contend with each other as rivals to be the best and most desirable. The sentiment is similar to VII.26.4 mithast├║ra ┼лt├бyo y├бsya p┼лrv─л╠Бс╕е тАЬwhose many forms of help compete for the lead,тАЭ meaning that they are all eager to be the most helpful.

The loc. sg. pr├бpatheс╣гu is taken by all standard tr. as тАЬon (your) journeysтАЭ (vel sim.), agreeing with the endpoint of GrassmannтАЩs def. тАШin die Ferne f├╝hrender Weg, Reise in die Ferne, ReiseтАЩ, which seems to me to follow a slippery path indeed. I interpr. the stem pr├бpatha- (4x) rather as lit. тАШthe path forwardтАЩ, but figuratively as тАШvanguardтАЩ. The -in-stem superlative prapath├нntama-, found nearby at I.173.7, then means тАШmost in the vanguardтАЩ (/тАЩmost forward on the pathтАЩ), used of Indra there and VI.31.5 (the 3rd occurrence, at VIII.1.30, is a PN). Although the difference between тАШjourneyтАЩ and тАШvanguardтАЩ is not crucial in our passage here, the two non-PN occurrences of prapath├нntama- both refer to Indra, with I.173.7 specifically to Indra as warrior, and тАШmost in the vanguardтАЩ works much better than RenouтАЩs тАЬtoi qui (vas) les grands chemins par excellenceтАЭ or Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬder am meisten auf dem Weg bist.тАЭ GeldnerтАЩs тАЬder am meisten auf der KriegsfahrtтАЭ seems to recognize this. For pr├бpatheс╣гu here IтАЩd be inclined to emend my published translation to тАЬon the paths forward,тАЭ because of the plural.

What is going on in d depends on the interpr. of sam├бy─Б, for which see comm. ad I.113.10. Most take it to mean тАШin the middleтАЩ vel sim.; this certainly produces an acceptable image, since the axle is between the two wheels. But as discussed ad I.113.10, the totality of passages containing sam├бy─Б suggest a meaning тАШaltogether, all at once, at the same timeтАЩ, and in all these passages it contrasts with a form of v├н (as here). The image I see here is somewhat more complex than the standard one, namely that through the action of the axle the wheels, though separate, turn at the same time. This is close to the kind of paradox much loved by RVic poets. This interpr. requires medial v─Бvс╣Ыte to be transitive (rather than intransitive-reflexive, pace most tr. and also K├╝mmel 464), but the self-involved nature of the action (the axle is turning its own wheels, as it were) makes this unproblematic. Potentially more troubling is that by this interpr. cakr─Б╠Бshould be dual acc., and the stem cakr├б- is neuter, whose dual should be (and several times is) cakr├й. However, in at least one passage, VIII.5.29, we have a clear masculine dual: ubh─Б╠Бcakr─Б╠Бhiraс╣Зy├бy─Б тАЬboth your wheels are goldenтАЭ (note the тАШbothтАЩ ubh─Б╠Б), which would match the form here.

Alternatively, we could take cakr─Б╠Бas neut. plural, assuming four wheels – and though this would technically require two axles, тАЬthe axleтАЭ as a mechanical marvel could stand for both. (Rather like saying тАЬthe internal-combustion engine powers most of the cars on the highway,тАЭ even though every car has its own.)

рддреЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдирд░реНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рдирд░реЗрднреНрдпреЛ рд╣рд┐рддреЗрд╖реБ рдмрд╛рд╣реБрд╖реБ рднреБрдЬреЗрд╖реБ рднреВрд░реАрдгрд┐ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрд╛рдирд┐ рднрджреНрд░рд╛ рднрджреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдирд┐ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпреЛ рджрд╛рддреБрдВ рдзрд┐рд░реЗ рджрдзрд┐рд░реЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╡рдХреНрд╖рдГрд╕реБ рдЙрд░рдГрд╕реНрдерд▓реЗрд╖реБ рд░реБрдХреНрдорд╛рдГ рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрд░рддреНрдирд╛рджрд┐рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд┐рддрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рднрд░рдгрд╛рдирд┐ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рд╛рдирд┐ ред рд░рднрд╕рд╛рд╕рдГ рд░рд╛рднрд╕реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдордиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЕрдЮреНрдЬрдпрдГ рд╡реНрдпрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ ред рдЕрдВрд╕реЗрд╖реБ рднреБрдЬрдореВрд▓реЗрд╖реБ рдПрддрд╛рдГ рд╢реБрдХреНрд▓рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛ рдорд╛рд▓рд╛рдГ ред рдкрд╡рд┐рд╖реБ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рд╕рджреГрд╢реЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рдпреБрдзреЗрд╖реБ рдХреНрд╖реБрд░рд╛рдГ рдХреНрд╖реБрд░рдзрд╛рд░рд╛рдГред рдЕрдзрд┐ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореНрдпрд░реНрдерд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджреА ред рдПрд╡рдореЗрддреЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЩреНрдЧреЗрд╖реБ рд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореАрдГ рдЕрдиреБрдХреНрд░рдореЗрдг рд╡рд┐ рдзрд┐рд░реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдВ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рд╡рдпреЛ рди рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдиреН рдкрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрдГ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдирд┐рд╡ рее рее реи рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, in your arms, propitious to man, are many good things; on your breasts are golden (ornaments) brilliant and conspicuous; while garlands (hang) on your shoulders; sharp are (the edges of) your weapons; the Maruts have various decorations, as birds have (many-coloured) wings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Many good things are on your manly arms, on your breasts brilliants, dazzling ornaments,
on your shoulders antelope (skins), on your wheel-rims razors. Like birds their wings, your splendors have spread out.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The adj. rabhas├б- ordinarily characterizes action (тАШviolent, frenziedтАЩ), but here must have a visual aspect. So also III.31.12. Such synaesthesia is not uncommon in the RV.

In d all standard tr. supply тАШtheyтАЩ [=Maruts] as subject of (vy ├бnu) dhire, with ┼Ыr├нyaс╕е as object (e.g., Geldner тАЬтАж haben sie ihre Herrlichkeiten entfaltetтАЭ). This amounts to a change of person, for these same tr. identify the many good things of a-c as тАШyoursтАЩ [=Maruts], following similar statements in vs. 9 with vaс╕е (a, cd). Though there are no overt 2nd ps. pronouns in vs. 10, the voc. marutaс╕е in p─Бda shows that 2nd ps. reference continues in this verse. Rather than changing person in d, I see another ex. of case disharmony between frame and simile, which is facilitated by the middle voice of dhire. The simile v├бyo n├б pakс╣г─Б╠Бn тАЬlike birds their wingsтАЭ uses the middle in transitive but self-involved sense, but, in my reading, in the frame dhire is intransitive, with ┼Ыr├нyaс╕е as subject. I must admit, however, that the person switches to 3rd in vs. 11, so that a switch here in the last p─Бda of 10 is not impossible. I prefer my interpr., with constant 2nd ps. in vs. 10, both because – all things being equal – itтАЩs best to keep verses self-contained and, more important, because Agastya likes doing tricky things with similes.

Griffith

Held in your manly arms are many goodly things, gold chains are on your chests, and glistering ornaments,
Deer-skins are on their shoulders, on their fellies knives: they spread their glory out as birds spread out their wings.

Geldner

Viele Sch├╢ne Sachen sind in euren m├дnnlichen Armen, auf eurer Brust Goldm├╝nzen, grelle Zierrate, auf den Schultern Antilopenfelle, an den Radschienen Messer. Wie V├╢gel die Fl├╝gel haben sie ihre Herrlichkeiten entfaltet.

Grassmann

In euern starken Armen ist viel sch├╢nes Gut, an euren Br├╝sten Goldgeh├дnge, blanker Schmuck, Auf Schultern Felle, Messer an der R├дder Rand; sie breiten Glanz wie V├╢gel ihre Schwingen aus.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдирд░реНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рднреВрд░реАрдгрд┐ рднрджреНрд░рд╛ рдмрд╛рд╣реБрд╖реБ рд╡рдХреНрд╖рдГрд╕реБрдГ рд░реБрдХреНрдорд╛ рдЕрдВрд╕реЗрд╖реНрд╡реЗрддрд╛ рд░рднрд╕рд╛рд╕реЛрд╜рдЮреНрдЬрдпрдГ рдкрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрд╡рдзрд┐рдХреНрд╖реБрд░рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдиреНрддреЗ рд╡рдпрдГ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдиреН рди рд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпреЛ рд╡реНрдпрдиреБ рдзрд┐рд░реЗ рее резреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

’ ( рдР. рдмреНрд░рд╛. рей. реиреж ) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рд╕реНрддреЛрднрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, mighty with mighty power, all-pervading, manifest afar off, as the gods (are made manifest) by the constellations; exhilarating, soft-tongued, speaking genitive ly with your mouths, associated with Indra, glorified by praise; (come to our sacrifice).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Great by their greatness, extending, extensive, visible from afar like the heavenly (realms) with their stars,
gladdening, good with their tongues, sounding with their mouths, the Maruts, linked to Indra, encircling him with their rhythm.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I have not rendered the y├й in b because in this verb-less string of nominal qualifiers it is difficult to decide where the relative clause ends and the main clause begins. (Both Renou and Witzel Got┼Н take d as the main cl.; Geldner seems to take it as cd, insofar as I can interpret his punctuation.) Alternatively, the whole vs. could be a relative clause hanging off vs. 10, or more specifically 10d. This structure would support the change of person in 10d seen by most tr., as opposed to my interpr., for which see immed. above.

Griffith

Mighty in mightiness, pervading, passing strong, visible from afar as ’twere with stars of heaven,
Lovely with pleasant tongues, sweet singers with their mouths, the Maruts, joined with Indra, shout forth all around.

Geldner

Die gro├Я sind an Gr├╢├Яe, m├дchtig, weitreichend, weithin sichtbar wie die himmlischen durch die Sterne; wohlklingende, zungenfertige T├╢ner mit dem Munde sind die Marut, dem Indra gesellt als sein Umjauchzer.

Grassmann

An Gr├╢sse gross und m├дchtig an gewalt’ger Macht, und weithin leuchtend Sternen gleich am Himmelsraum, Sch├╢nzungig, munter, lustig rauschend mit dem Mund, vereint mit Indra jubelt rings die Marutschar.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ рдорд╣реНрдирд╛ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рднреНрд╡реЛ рд╡рд┐рднреВрддрдпреЛ рджреВрд░реЗрджреГрд╢ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЗ рд╕рдВрдорд┐рд╢реНрд▓рд╛ рд╕реНрддреГрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднреЛ рдорд░реБрддреЛ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЗрд╡ рдордиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдГ рд╕рдиреНрдд рдЖрд╕рднрд┐рд░рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдпрдиреНрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢рдиреНрддрд┐ рдЪ рддреЗ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд▓рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдЬрд╛рдпрдиреНрддреЗ рее резрез рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSuch, well-born Maruts, is your greatness, that your munificence is as long (continued) as the function of Aditi; and Indra does not exceed, by his own liberality, (the value of) that which you have bestowed upon the devout man (who worships you).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Aditer iva vratam, the act or obligation of Aditi, either the mother of the gods, or the earth

Jamison Brereton

This is your greatness, o well-born Maruts: your gift is long(-lasting), like the commandment of Aditi.
For the person of good action to whom you gave it, not even Indra
makes it go awry through dereliction.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. has ties to earlier parts of the hymn. The opening t├бd vaс╕е тАж mahitvan├бm тАЬthis is your greatnessтАЭ echoes 1ab t├бn n├║ voc─Бma тАж mahitv├бm. There it was their previous (p┼л╠Бrvam) greatness; this vs. presumably brings this greatness into the present time.

P─Бda b seems a paraphrase of 7a anavabhr├бr─Бdhasaс╕е тАШwhose gifts are not withdrawnтАЩ.

The connection between the main clause and the relative clause in cd is somewhat loose: as a correlative to the rel. cl. j├бn─Бya y├бsmai тАЬfor whatever personтАЭ we would expect t├бm, not t├бd, which must refer to the gift, not the recipient of it.

Griffith

This is your majesty, ye Maruts nobly born, far as the sway of Aditi your bounty spreads.
Even Indra by desertion never disannuls the boon bestowed by you upon the pious man.

Geldner

Das ist eure Gr├╢├Яe, ihr edelgeborenen Marut: eure Gabe ist dauernd wie das Gebot der Aditi. Auch Indra macht sie nicht aus Feindschaft dem frommen Mann abwendig, dem ihr sie geschenkt habt.

Grassmann

Das ist, o edle Maruts, eure Herrlichkeit, weit reicht eur Geben wie der Aditi Gesetz; Auch Indra selbst verletzt mit seinem Angriff nicht, das, was dem frommen Manne ihr gew├дhret habt.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд╡реЛ рдЬрд╛рдорд┐рддреНрд╡рдВ рдмрдиреНрдзреБрддреНрд╡рдорд╕реНрдорджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдкреНрд░реЗрдорд╛рдзрд┐рдХреНрдпрдВ рддрддреН рдЦрд▓реБ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рдХрд┐рдпрддреНрдкрд░реНрдпрдиреНрддрдорд┐рддрд┐ рддрджреБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдкрд░реЗ рдпреБрдЧреЗ ред рдпреБрдЧрд╢рдмреНрджрдГ рдХрд╛рд▓реЛрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдХрдГ ред рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗ рдорд╣рддрд┐ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗрд╜рддреАрддреЗрд╜рдкрд┐ рд╡рд░реНрддрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рддрддреНрдХрдердордзрд┐рдЧрддрдорд┐рддреНрдпрдд рдЖрд╣ ред рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рд╕рдГ рдЕрдорд░рдгрдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдгреЛ рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдпрддреН рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рд╢рдВрд╕рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдВ рдкреБрд░реБ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрдВ рдпрдерд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдЖрд╡рдд рд░рдХреНрд╖рде ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреНрдпреБрд╖реНрдорддреНрдХреГрддрдВ рдЬрд╛рдорд┐рддреНрд╡рдорд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢реАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдпреВрдпрдореН рдЕрдпрд╛ рдзрд┐рдпрд╛ рдЕрдирдпрд╛рдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рддреНрдорд┐рдХрдпрд╛ рдмреБрджреНрдзреНрдпрд╛ рдордирд╡реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдп рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗ рдпрд╖реНрдЯреНрд░реЗ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрд╛рджрдпреЗ рд╢реНрд░реБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдорд╛рд╡реНрдп рдХреАрд░реНрддрд┐рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдВ рд╡рд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рдВрднреВрдп рдирд░рдГ рдиреЗрддрд╛рд░рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ рджрдВрд╕рдиреИрдГред рдХрд░реНрдорднрд┐рд░рд┐рддреНрдердВрднреВрддрд╛рдГ рдЖ рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреНрд░рд┐рд░реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рдЬрд╛рдиреАрде рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour alliance with us, Maruts, is of a long duration on which account, immortals, accept our ample praise and, having accepted ourlaudation, be gratified, leaders (of sacrifice), by our holy acts, through this (your) favourable disposition towards mankind.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This is your kinship to the earlier generation, o Maruts, that as
immortals you many times favored its laud.
By reason of this poetic insight (of ManuтАЩs), having favored his
attentive hearing, the superior men [=Maruts] showed themselves to Manu all at once through their wondrous deeds.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take cd as a concrete example of the statement in ab, that the MarutsтАЩ connection with the older generation arises from their favoring its тАЬlaudтАЭ (┼Ы├бс╣Гsam – note that this positively viewed ┼Ы├бс╣Гsa- contrasts with the evil ┼Ы├бс╣Гsa- of 8d). Manu is of course a member of the older generation, and because of his тАЬinsightтАЭ (ay─Б╠Бdhiy─Б╠Б) the Maruts favor him and show themselves to him with all their wondrous qualities.

Griffith

This is your kinship, Maruts, that, Immortals, ye were oft in olden time regardful of our call,
Having vouchsafed to man a hearing through this prayer, by wondrous deeds the Heroes have displayed their might.

Geldner

Das war, o Marut, euer Verwandtschaftsgef├╝hl in einer fernen Zeit, da├Я ihr Unsterbliche oftmals das Preislied bevorzugtet. Mit dieser Gesinnung haben die Herren sich vor Manu, seine Dienstwilligkeit bevorzugend, zugleich mit ihren Meisterk├╝nsten sehen lassen.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬQuick-moving Maruts, we augment the long (offered ceremony) upon your mighty (approach), whereby men triumph in war; may we obtain, by these our sacrifices, your wished-for (presence).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The abundance stemming from you, o powerful MarutsтАФthrough which we shall stay powerfully swollen for a long time,
toward which the people in the community will stretch outтАФto that might I attain, *to my desire, with these sacrifices.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The relations among the clauses in this vs. might be problematic, primarily because of an apparent gender mismatch: p├бr─лс╣Зas- тАШabundanceтАЩ, which in the instr.

p├бr─лс╣Зas─Б goes with the rel. y├йna in the rel. clause occupying ab, would be the most likely referent of both y├бd in the parallel rel. clause of c and t├бd in the main clause of d. And in fact that is how I (and the other standard tr.) take it. However, p├бr─лс╣Зas- is said to be masculine and y├бd/t├бd are of course neuter – an obstacle that Oldenberg for his part considers too large to be overcome. However, the noun is most likely neuter.

This is what weтАЩd expect of a stem built with suffix -nas-, and the only diagnostic form for a masc. is acc. sg. p├бr─лс╣Зasam in III.24.5. Otherwise the forms are singular obliques, esp. in the collocation r─Бy─Б╠Бp├бr─лс╣Зas─Б тАЬwith wealth in profusionтАЭ (4x), and hence ambiguous as to gender. The masc. acc. sg. is most probably a nonce form created to match its usual formulaic partner, masc. ray├н-, in the phrase ray├нс╣Г v─лr├бvantam p├бr─лс╣Зasam. See AiG II.2.738 and EWA s.v. Substantially the same argument is made by Lubotsky (тАЬAvestan xv ar╟Эnah-: The Etymology and Concept, 1998, 483).

abh─л╠Бс╣гс╣нim in d is analyzed by the Pp. as abh├н ├нс╣гс╣нim, as might be expected. Since (vanishingly rare) root-accented ├нс╣гс╣нi- is derived from тИЪyaj and means тАШsacrificeтАЩ, the standard tr. exert a good deal of effort to introduce this sacrifice into their interpretation, somewhat embarassingly in a p─Бda that already contains ebh├нr yaj├▒├йbhiс╕е тАЬwith these sacrifices.тАЭ Cf. RenouтАЩs rather overblown тАЬpuiss├й-je l’obtenir gr├вce aux sacrifices que voici, pour (que vous soyez pr├йsents ├а mon) oblationтАЭ (the тАЬlтАЩтАЭ in тАЬlтАЩobtenirтАЭ is the p├бr─лс╣Зas-). I take it rather to iс╣гс╣н├н- тАШdesireтАЩ, in a phrase abh├н

*iс╣гt├нm тАЬto my desire, to my likingтАЩ. Either the annealed sandhi form *abh─л╠Бс╣гt├нс╣Г lost its 2nd accent redactionally, or the accent retraction that was ultimately to affect all -tistems (see Lundquist, -ti-stems) was already spreading to this stem, producing the occasional ├нс╣гс╣нi- тАШdesireтАЩ.

Griffith

That, O ye Maruts, we may long time flourish through your abundant riches, O swift movers,
And that our men may spread in the encampment, let me complete the rite with these oblations.

Lasst, starke Maruts, eures Reichthums F├╝lle mich, durch welche wir gedeihen m├╢gen lange Zeit, Als eure Gunst erlangen durch dies Opferwerk, und dass sich weit verbreite unser Volk im Land.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis praise, Maruts, is for you; this hymn is for you; (the work) of a venerable author, capable of conferring (by his laudations); may the praise reach you (for the good of your) person ns, so that we may thence obtain food, strength, and long life.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Here is a praise for you, o Maruts, here a hymn from M─Бnd─Бrya, the respectful bard.
With refreshment he would beg propitiation for himself. тАУ May we
know refreshment and a community having lively waters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This signature verse of AgastyaтАЩs Indra/Marut hymns appears in I.165.15, 166.15, 167.11, and 168.10, but not in all of his Triс╣гс╣нubh hymns even to Indra. The tr.

of I.165.15 (JPB) differs somewhat from the others (SWJ). JPB interprets m─Бny├б- as a patronymic to a PN m─Б╠Бna-, while I take it as an adj. тАШrespectfulтАЩ derived from m─Б╠Бna- тАШrespectтАЩ. It is possible that both are meant.

Both tr. follow Oldenberg in reading тАШvay─Б╠Бm тАШpropitiationтАЩ (SWJ) / тАШreconciliationтАЩ (JPB) for vay─Б╠Бm. This requires no emendation to the Saс╣Гhit─Б text, only to the Pp. My tr. should, however, have an asterisk before тАШpropitiationтАЩ in all three cases.

Griffith

May this your laud, may this your song, O Maruts, sung by the poet, Mana’s son, Mandarya,
Bring offspring for ourselves with food to feed us. May we find strengthening food in full abundance.

Geldner

Dies Preislied, diese Lobrede des Dichters Mandarya, des Maniden, ist f├╝r euch, Marut. Er m├╢chte durch Nahrungsf├╝lle f├╝r seine Person zu Nachwuchs gelangen. - Wir m├╢chten einen gastfreien Opferb├╝ndler kennen lernen, der rasch schenkt.

Grassmann

Euch, Maruts, gilt dies Lied des Manasohnes, das Lob des Dichters von dem Stamm Mand─Бra’s, Mit Labung kommt herbei zu eigner St├дrkung gebt Labung uns und wasserreiche Fluren.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддреЛ рд╡реЛ рдп рдПрд╖ рд╕реНрддреЛрдореЛ рдорд╛рдиреНрджрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдХрд╛рд░реЛрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рдЧреАрд░реНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрддреЗ рдпрд╛рдВ рддрдиреНрд╡реЗ рдЗрд╖рд╛ рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рджрд╛рдпрд╛рд╕реАрд╖реНрдЯ рддрд╛рдорд┐рд╖рдВ рд╡реГрдЬрдирдВ рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдЮреНрдЪ рд╡рдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо рее резрел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрд╖рдГ) (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╕реНрддреЛрдордГ) рд╕реНрддрд╡рдирдореН (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ (рдЗрдпрдореН) (рдЧреАрдГ) рд╡рд╛рдгреА (рдорд╛рдиреНрджрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд┐рдиреЛ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХрд╕реНрдп (рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рд╕рддреНрдХрд░реНрддреНрддреБрдВ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрд╕реНрдп (рдХрд╛рд░реЛрдГ) рдкреНрд░рдпрддрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп (рдЖ) (рдЗрд╖рд╛) рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдпрд╛ (рдпрд╛рд╕реАрд╖реНрдЯ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН (рддрдиреНрд╡реЗ) рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рдп (рд╡рдпрд╛рдореН) рд╡рдпрдореНред рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрдирд╛рд╜рддреНрд░ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдо (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рдЕрдиреНрдирдореН (рд╡реГрдЬрдирдореН) рдмрд▓рдореН (рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдореН) рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореН рее резрел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЖрдкреНрддрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рддреНрдордмрд▓рдВ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдВ рдЬреАрд╡рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддрд┐ рее резрел реердЕрддреНрд░ рдорд░реБрджреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддрд┐ рд╖рдЯреНрд╖рд╖реНрдЯреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рддреГрддреАрдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдЪреА рд╕реНрддреБрддреА рдХрд░реВрди рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮ рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдореНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреА рд╡рд╛рдгреА рдРрдХреВрди, рд╢рд░реАрд░ рд╡ рдЖрддреНрдореНрдпрд╛рдЪреЗ рдмрд▓ рд╡рд╛рдврд╡реВрди рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рдпреВ рдмрдирд▓реЗ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ. рее резрел рее
